## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), dissipative forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and driven oscillators provide the relevant formula structures.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Generalized Duffing-van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Softening/hardening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic restoring)
- Coulomb-like friction oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * v**2)**(-1) (nonlinear friction model)
- Position-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (damping proportional to displacement)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential / broken symmetry in restoring force
- Velocity-dependent terms with x**2*v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillations (van der Pol type)
- Cubic velocity terms (v**3) → nonlinear dissipation distinguishing Rayleigh from van der Pol oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Product terms x*v → position-velocity coupling indicating non-conservative or gyroscopic-like forces
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Negative linear damping coefficient with positive nonlinear damping → limit cycle behavior (self-sustained oscillation)

For v>0, `log(exp(v)+1) ≈ v` for large v, while `log(|v|+1) = log(v+1)` grows logarithmically. These are fundamentally different. Also, none of these have `sin(v)`.

**GT:** `-0.118064*v*(1 - x²) - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Expanding: `0.118064*v*x² - 1.00534*v - 0.118064*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`
= `0.118064*v*x² - 1.12340*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

The GT contains these basis functions/terms:
1. `v*x²` - product of v and x²
2. `v` - linear in v
3. `log(|v| + 1)` - logarithm involving |v|
4. `sin(t)` - sine of t
5. `sin(v)` - sine of v

Key observations:
- The GT has `sin(v)` and `log(|v|+1)` which are nonlinear functions of v
- The GT has `sin(t)` (time-dependent)
- The GT has `v*x²` coupling term
- No explicit `x` term (only through `v*x²`)
- No `cos(t)` term

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(v)` and `log(|v|+1)`:

**Critical filter:** The GT requires both `sin(v)` and `log(|v|+1)`. These are specific nonlinear functions of `v` that cannot be replicated by polynomials, exponentials of `v²`, or other basis functions. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, any candidate lacking these terms cannot match.

Let me scan all candidates:

- **Candidates 1-4:** Have `log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1)` which is a softplus function. This equals `log(exp(c8*v) + 1/c7) + log(c7)`. For large negative v, softplus → 0; for large positive v, softplus → c8*v. This is NOT equivalent to `log(|v|+1)` which is symmetric in v. Also, none have `sin(v)`. **NO MATCH** for all.

- **Candidates 5-50:** None contain `sin(v)` or `log(|v|+1)`. They use combinations of polynomials in v (v, v², v³), exponentials (exp(v²)), trigonometric functions of t, and polynomial/product terms in x. None can reproduce the `sin(v)` term or the `log(|v|+1)` term.

By linear independence, `sin(v)` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of `v`, `v³`, `exp(v²)`, `v/(a+bv²)`, or other basis functions present in the candidates. Similarly, `log(|v|+1)` cannot be expressed by these basis functions.

Let me verify candidates 1-4 more carefully regarding `log(c7*exp(c8*v)+1)`:
- This is NOT symmetric in v, while `log(|v|+1)` IS symmetric
- Even if we could somehow approximate one nonlinear v-function, we still need `sin(v)` which no candidate has

**Every single candidate is missing `sin(v)`, which is a required basis function in the GT.** No combination of the available terms (polynomials in v, exp(v²), softplus, etc.) can exactly equal `sin(v)` for all v.
